28/05/24, 10:09 - Sritama Makaut: #include<stdio.h>
int main()
{
int n,i=1,sum=0;
printf("Enter a number: ");
scanf("%d",&n);
while(i<n)
{
if(n%i==0)
sum=sum+i;
i++;
}
if(sum==n)
printf("%d is a perfect number",i);
else
printf("%d is not a perfect number",i);
return 0;
}

“The government's sudden enforcement of the lockdown seemed hastily prepared and immediately disadvantaged already vulnerable populations. ChatGPT
(a) In light of the above passage, does the decision by the Government seem justified?
The government's decision to enforce a sudden lockdown was justified from a public health perspective, as it aimed to curb the rapid spread of COVID-19, a virus that posed a severe threat to human life. However, the execution of the lockdown appears poorly planned and lacked foresight, particularly in addressing the needs of vulnerable populations such as migrant workers and those in the informal economy. A more balanced and well-prepared approach could have mitigated the socio-economic hardships caused by the lockdown. Thus, while the intent was justified, the implementation was not.

(b) While curbing the spread of the disease on one hand and heralding mass economic crisis on the other, was it a ‘lesser wrong,’ and why?
The lockdown can be considered a "lesser wrong" because the immediate priority was to save lives in the face of an unprecedented health crisis. Allowing the virus to spread unchecked could have overwhelmed the healthcare system, leading to catastrophic loss of life. However, the economic crisis triggered by the lockdown disproportionately impacted vulnerable populations, highlighting the ethical dilemma of choosing between public health and economic stability. It was a difficult trade-off, and while lives were prioritized over livelihoods, better planning and communication could have reduced the extent of economic and social suffering.

(c) Was the action of imposing lockdown a utilitarian decision or a deontological one? Explain.
The decision to impose a lockdown was largely utilitarian in nature, as it sought to achieve the greatest good for the greatest number of people by prioritizing public health over individual freedoms and economic stability. The utilitarian framework justified the restriction of movement and economic activity to prevent the spread of the virus, thereby protecting the majority from severe health risks and potential fatalities.

However, from a deontological perspective, the suddenness of the lockdown and its disregard for the immediate welfare of vulnerable groups violated moral obligations to protect all citizens, particularly those most in need. A deontological approach would have emphasized planning and protecting these groups regardless of the broader utilitarian outcomes.

(d) Could there be a deontological solution for paving a way to resist the pandemic in view of the plight of the masses working in the informal economy? Validate your argument.
A deontological solution would focus on the moral duty to protect the inherent rights and dignity of every individual, particularly the vulnerable. Such a solution could include:

Advance Notice and Preparation: Announcing the lockdown with sufficient lead time to allow migrant workers to return home and informal workers to secure basic needs.
Financial and Food Security Measures: Ensuring direct cash transfers, food distribution, and healthcare access for informal workers and daily wage earners to reduce their suffering.
Localized Containment: Implementing localized restrictions in hotspots rather than a blanket lockdown, thus minimizing disruptions to livelihoods while curbing virus spread.
Public Communication and Transparency: Clear communication of plans and rationale behind measures to build trust and cooperation among the public.
These measures align with deontological ethics by respecting the rights and dignity of vulnerable populations without compromising the broader goal of pandemic resistance. Balancing these ethical obligations with public health needs could ensure a more equitable and humane response.

02/12/24, 16:34 - +91 79808 40728: To generalize the square root function into a function that calculates the \(p\)th root of a number \(x\) with a tolerable error \(e\), you can use an iterative method like the **Newton-Raphson method** or binary search. Here's how you can implement this in Python:

### Code Implementation
```python
def getroot(x, p, e):
    """
    Finds the pth root of x within an error tolerance of e.
    
    Parameters:
    x : float : The number whose root is to be found
    p : int   : The root to be calculated (e.g., p=2 for square root)
    e : float : Tolerable error
    
    Returns:
    float : The pth root of x
    """
    if x < 0 and p % 2 == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot calculate even root of a negative number.")
    
    # Initial guess
    guess = x if x >= 1 else 1.0

    while True:
        # Newton-Raphson formula for pth root
        next_guess = ((p - 1) * guess + x / (guess ** (p - 1))) / p
        if abs(next_guess - guess) < e:
            return next_guess
        guess = next_guess
```

### Explanation:
1. **Input Parameters:**
   - `x`: The number for which the \(p\)th root is calculated.
   - `p`: The degree of the root (e.g., \(p = 2\) for square root, \(p = 3\) for cube root).
   - `e`: Tolerable error, determining the accuracy of the result.

2. **Algorithm:**
   - Use the **Newton-Raphson formula** to iteratively refine the estimate for the root.
   - Stop when the difference between consecutive guesses is less than \(e\).

3. **Handling Edge Cases:**
   - \(x < 0\): If \(x\) is negative and \(p\) is even, raise an error since the result would not be real.
   - Small values of \(x\): Ensure convergence with an appropriate initial guess.

### Example Usage
```python
print(getroot(27, 3, 0.0001))  # Cube root of 27
print(getroot(16, 4, 0.0001))  # Fourth root of 16
print(getroot(0.001, 3, 0.0001))  # Cube root of 0.001
```

This function is efficient and handles arbitrary roots and errors with precision.

31/12/24, 10:47 - Madhusudan Singh Makaut: Read the Problem carefully and answer the question (s) that follow:
As the General Manager of XYZ Co Ltd, you have been assigned a team of ten people and given a task which is to be completed within a deadline of ten days. On the eighth day, one of your team members who was assigned a vital task requests a leave on grounds of bereavement due to the death of a close one. Your company has hitherto endorsed the culture of firing people who are regarded inept. In this scenario, you have but two options at hand:
Option A: Hire a new person to get the job done and fire the existing employee.
Option B: Seek an extension of the deadline even if it means that you, as team leader have to take the onus.
(a)	As a team leader, which option would you choose and why?
(b)	How would you justify your decision before the higher authority in your company?
(c)	What are the cons associated with the decision which you did not take? Justify your answer.

08/01/25, 23:13 - Sritama Makaut: Read the Problem carefully and answer the question (s) that follow:
As the General Manager of XYZ Co Ltd, you have been assigned a team of ten people and given a task which is to be completed within a deadline of ten days. On the eighth day, one of your team members who was assigned a vital task requests a leave on grounds of bereavement due to the death of a close one. Your company has hitherto endorsed the culture of firing people who are regarded inept. In this scenario, you have but two options at hand:
Option A: Hire a new person to get the job done and fire the existing employee.
Option B: Seek an extension of the deadline even if it means that you, as team leader have to take the onus.
(a)	As a team leader, which option would you choose and why?
(b)	How would you justify your decision before the higher authority in your company?
(c)	What are the cons associated with the decision which you did not take? Justify your answer.

11/02/25, 02:09 - Ritochit Ghosh Makaut: To ,
The Vice Chancellor
MAKAUT
Nadia, Haringhata
741249
Date: 10/02/2025
Subject: Concern regarding inadequate facilities during emergency situations.
Respected Sir,
We are writing to express our deep shock, frustration, and anger regarding the tragic incident 
involving one of our students, Sayani Sen, a first-year M.Tech student in VLSI. It is with great sorrow 
that we inform you of her suicide today, 10/02/2025, but the shocking part of this incident is the 
complete negligence and gross inefficiency exhibited by the authorities and staff responsible for the 
safety and well-being of the students.
Sayani went missing for an extended period of time, and despite her mother searching for her across 
the campus for almost two hours, there was no assistance from the security personnel or any 
university staff to help locate her. It is highly distressing to think that no one in the university took 
any responsibility for ensuring the safety of the student during this time. Ultimately she was found 
at around 7 PM at very terrible condition at the back of academic building near the generator and 
her pulse was still going on.
Further compounding this tragedy was the complete failure of the university's emergency services. 
The university ambulance, which is supposed to be available 24 hours, was not readily accessible to 
the students. This, despite the fact that Sayani was still alive and we, the students of MAKAUT tried 
to get access for public transport which took almost 20 minutes. The students, then managed to 
arrange for a toto rickshaw, but by the time they reached the hospital, it was too late, the girl passed 
away.
Additionally, the problem regarding the ambulance was also complained earlier but no action has 
been taken.
This incident raises serious concerns about the overall management and security systems of the 
university. It is not enough to blame just the security personnel and drivers. This is a systemic failure
that reflects poorly on the administration and the management's lack of responsibility in ensuring 
student safety. The lack of communication, coordination, and proper management of emergency 
resources is appalling. This cannot be brushed aside as a one-time error. The higher authorities, 
including relevant administrative personnel, are all accountable for this horrific chain of events. `
The students also asked the security to call the Higher Authorities multiple times but they directly 
denied and after that we took some actions to draw their attention to this matter.
We strongly urge you, as the Vice Chancellor, to investigate this matter thoroughly and take 
appropriate action against all those responsible. This tragedy should not be reduced to just another 
news report. It is imperative that all systems related to student safety and emergency services are 
urgently reviewed and improved. The university must ensure the prompt and efficient response to 
emergencies and must guarantee that such a senseless loss of life never occurs again.
We expect nothing short of a full investigation and accountability from the university’s management. 
The failure to act appropriately in this case is unacceptable, and we demand immediate attention to 
this matter.
Yours sincerely,
Students of MAKAUT

24/03/25, 14:50 - Ⓕαяђ𝒶ภ: #include<stdio.h>
void bubblesort(double a[],int n){
  for(int i=1;i<=n-1;i++){
    for(int j=1;j<=n-i;j++){
      if(a[j]>=a[j+1]){
        double temp = a[j];
        a[j] = a[j+1];
        a[j+1]=temp;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  
  int main(){
    int n;
    printf("Enter number of element: ");
    scanf("%d",&n);
    double a[n+1];
    printf("Enter %d element for your array: ",n);
    for(int i=1;i<=n;i++){
      scanf("%lf",&a[i]);
      }
      bubblesort(a,n);
      printf("Sorted array: ");
      for(int i=1;i<=n;i++){
      printf("%.2lf ",a[i]);
      }
      printf("\n");
      return 0;
    }
24/03/25, 14:50 - Ⓕαяђ𝒶ภ: #include<stdio.h>
void selectionsort(double a[],int n){
  for(int i=1;i<=n;i++){
    int j=i;
    for(int k = j+1;k<=n;k++){
      if(a[k]<a[j]) j=k;
      }
      if(j != i){
        double temp=a[i];
        a[i]=a[j];
        a[j]=temp;
        }
    }
  }
  
  int main(){
    int n;
    printf("Enter number of element: ");
    scanf("%d",&n);
    double a[n+1];
    printf("Enter %d element for your array: ",n);
    for(int i=1;i<=n;i++){
      scanf("%lf",&a[i]);
      }
      selectionsort(a,n);
      printf("Sorted array: ");
      for(int i=1;i<=n;i++){
      printf("%.2lf ",a[i]);
      }
      printf("\n");
      return 0;
    }

19/05/25, 14:25 - +91 76797 63617: *OS Lab Assignments on _pthreads_ (2025-05-19, 2025-05-20)*

You are to use pthread related functions such as ~pthread_create(3)~,
~pthread_join(3)~, ~pthread_exit(3)~, etc. to create threads,
synchronize and communicate data between threads, and terminate
threads (pthreads, or posix threads).

* Assignments for practice and to get familiar with pthreads

1. Write a C program where you will store an array of 10 strings.

#include <pthread.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <unistd.h>

#define NUM_STRINGS 10
#define MAX_LEN 100

char *strings[NUM_STRINGS] = {
    "String 1: Hello",
    "String 2: World",
    "String 3: This",
    "String 4: Is",
    "String 5: A",
    "String 6: Threaded",
    "String 7: String",
    "String 8: Printing",
    "String 9: Example",
    "String 10: Done"
};

// Thread function
void *print_string(void *arg) {
    int index = *(int *)arg;
    printf("Thread %d: %s\n", index, strings[index]);
    free(arg); // Prevent memory leak
    return NULL;
}

int main() {
    pthread_t threads[NUM_STRINGS];

    for (int i = 0; i < NUM_STRINGS; i++) {
        int *arg = malloc(sizeof(*arg));
        *arg = i;

        if (pthread_create(&threads[i], NULL, print_string, arg) != 0) {
            perror("Failed to create thread");
            return 1;
        }
    }

    // Wait for all threads to finish
    for (int i = 0; i < NUM_STRINGS; i++) {
        pthread_join(threads[i], NULL);
    }

    return 0;
}
19/05/25, 14:32 - +91 76797 63617: #include <stdio.h>
#include <pthread.h>
#include <time.h>

#define NUM_THREADS 5

void* thread_function(void* arg) {
    int thread_id = *(int*)arg;
    printf("Thread %d is running\n", thread_id);
    // Simulate some work
    for (volatile long i = 0; i < 100000000; ++i);
    return NULL;
}

int main() {
    pthread_t threads[NUM_THREADS];
    int thread_ids[NUM_THREADS];

    clock_t t_begin, t_end;
    double t_total;

    // Start timing
    t_begin = clock();

    // Create threads
    for (int i = 0; i < NUM_THREADS; ++i) {
        thread_ids[i] = i;
        if (pthread_create(&threads[i], NULL, thread_function, &thread_ids[i]) != 0) {
            perror("Failed to create thread");
            return 1;
        }
    }

    // Join threads
    for (int i = 0; i < NUM_THREADS; ++i) {
        if (pthread_join(threads[i], NULL) != 0) {
            perror("Failed to join thread");
            return 1;
        }
    }

    // Stop timing
    t_end = clock();
    t_total = ((double)(t_end - t_begin)) / CLOCKS_PER_SEC;

    printf("Total time taken by threads: %f seconds\n", t_total);

    return 0;
}

19/05/25, 14:36 - +91 76797 63617: #include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <pthread.h>
#include <time.h>

#define NUM_THREADS 10

// Thread function
void* thread_function(void* arg) {
    long tid = (long)arg;
    int* result = malloc(sizeof(int));
    if (result == NULL) {
        perror("Failed to allocate memory");
        pthread_exit(NULL);
    }

    // Generate random number between 0 and 99
    *result = rand() % 100;

    printf("Thread %ld: generated number %d\n", tid, *result);

    pthread_exit((void*)result);
}

int main() {
    pthread_t threads[NUM_THREADS];
    void* status;
    int sum = 0;

    // Seed the random number generator
    srand(time(NULL));

    // Create threads
    for (long i = 0; i < NUM_THREADS; ++i) {
        if (pthread_create(&threads[i], NULL, thread_function, (void*)i) != 0) {
            perror("pthread_create failed");
            exit(EXIT_FAILURE);
        }
    }

    // Join threads and collect results
    for (int i = 0; i < NUM_THREADS; ++i) {
        if (pthread_join(threads[i], &status) != 0) {
            perror("pthread_join failed");
            exit(EXIT_FAILURE);
        }
        int* result = (int*)status;
        sum += *result;
        free(result);  // Free allocated memory from thread
    }

    // Print the final summed value
    printf("Sum of all random numbers: %d\n", sum);

    return 0;
}
19/05/25, 14:37 - +91 76797 63617: #!/bin/bash

# Check if argument n is provided and is a positive integer
if ! [[ "$1" =~ ^[1-9][0-9]*$ ]]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <number_of_runs>"
    exit 1
fi

n=$1
total_time=0

# Make sure the executable exists
executable="./problem2_exec"
if [ ! -x "$executable" ]; then
    echo "Error: Executable '$executable' not found or not executable."
    exit 1
fi

echo "Running $executable $n times..."

for ((i = 1; i <= n; i++)); do
    # Capture the real time using /usr/bin/time
    run_time=$( { /usr/bin/time -f "%e" $executable > /dev/null; } 2>&1 )
    total_time=$(echo "$total_time + $run_time" | bc)
    echo "Run $i: ${run_time}s"
done

average=$(echo "scale=4; $total_time / $n" | bc)

echo "Average time over $n runs: ${average}s"
19/05/25, 14:38 - +91 76797 63617: #include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <pthread.h>
#include <time.h>

#define NUM_THREADS 10

int random_numbers[NUM_THREADS];       // Array to store random numbers
pthread_t threads[NUM_THREADS];        // Array to store thread identifiers

void* generate_random(void* arg) {
    int thread_id = *(int*)arg;
    random_numbers[thread_id] = rand() % 100; // Generate number between 0-99
    printf("Thread %d generated: %d\n", thread_id, random_numbers[thread_id]);
    free(arg);
    pthread_exit(NULL);
}

void* thread_zero(void* arg) {
    int sum = 0;

    // Wait for threads 1 through 9
    for (int i = 1; i < NUM_THREADS; i++) {
        pthread_join(threads[i], NULL);
        sum += random_numbers[i];
    }

    printf("Thread 0 calculated the sum: %d\n", sum);

    int* result = malloc(sizeof(int));
    *result = sum;
    pthread_exit(result);
}

int main() {
    srand(time(NULL));

    // Create threads 1 to 9
    for (int i = 1; i < NUM_THREADS; i++) {
        int* thread_id = malloc(sizeof(int));
        *thread_id = i;
        pthread_create(&threads[i], NULL, generate_random, thread_id);
    }

    // Create thread 0 last
    pthread_create(&threads[0], NULL, thread_zero, NULL);

    // Wait for thread 0 and collect sum
    int* total_sum;
    pthread_join(threads[0], (void**)&total_sum);
    printf("Total sum received by main: %d\n", *total_sum);

    free(total_sum);
    return 0;
}
